{"type": "text", "file": {"filePath": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_MQN7mBg4AhvH/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_research_1/research_out.json", "content": "{\n  \"title\": \"Spec Sheet: Label-Free FDR Gate at the LLM Text-to-Logic Admission Boundary\",\n  \"summary\": \"Consolidated, source-traceable implementation spec for the label-free decoy-competition FDR gate that admits LLM-extracted facts/bridges into a Prolog/symbolic layer. Provides, for each component, a verbatim formula (with equation number and source), a symbol glossary, a language-agnostic pseudo-procedure, and a recommended default. KEY RESULTS: (A) knockoff+ admission threshold T=min{t: (1+#{W_i<=-t})/(#{W_i>=t} v 1)<=alpha} (Barber-Candes eq 1.9, exact FDR via Thm 2; plain knockoff eq 1.8 controls only modified FDR Thm 1); the minimum-estimable-FDR floor is 1/k, so certifying FDR<=alpha needs k>=ceil(1/alpha) admissions -> demonstrable alpha grid {0.05,0.1,0.2,0.3,0.5} maps to k-floors {20,10,5,4,2}. Rajchert-Keich prove the '+1' is generally necessary (t=1 optimal), so keep it; TDC-SB/TDC-UB (bandsfdp) are an optional tighter FDX bound. (B) Entrapment estimators verbatim from Wen et al. 2025: combined FDP=N_E(1+1/r)/(N_T+N_E) (upper bound, DEFAULT), paired (eq4, requires r=1, tighter), lower bound N_E/(N_T+N_E) (failure-only), and 'sample' N_E(1/r)/N_T which is INVALID (biased). r=#entrapment/#target; default r=1 paired. (C) Document-block (cluster) bootstrap B>=2000 for all FDP/FDR CIs (resample whole documents; Cameron-Gelbach-Miller anchor) — the CI used by the primary disconfirmation. (D) Sole validity condition = Barber-Candes Lemma 1 (null W signs are i.i.d. fair coins) = TDC equal-chance; two anti-conservative failure modes (within-doc correlation -> bootstrap; batched contrast effect -> isolated provenance-blinded order-randomized scoring) and the isolated-vs-batched discriminator. (E) Property-matched document-conditioned COUNTERFACTUAL decoys + non-entailment verification (DeepCoy principle; DOE 0.166->0.032/0.109->0.038); random type-matched swaps kept as the anti-conservative negative control. (F) Ranked label-free upper-tail elicitation shortlist: DINCO (primary, overconfidence-corrected), FactSelfCheck (fact-level), self-consistency/SelfCheckGPT, logprob/yes-no-token (if exposed), verbalized (overconfident floor); Phase-0 selects on tail-AUC>0.5 with CI + isolated~batched agreement. (G) Recommended model openai/gpt-4.1-nano ($0.10/$0.40 per M, logprobs+auto-caching, <$0.30 input); fallbacks gpt-4o-mini then a logprob-free cheap caching model; projected cost ~$1-3 << $10 cap. (H) Novelty confirmed: no prior work applies knockoff/target-decoy/entrapment FDR at a label-free LLM text->logic admission boundary (conformal factuality/selection are labeled and certify outputs). Includes a final Parameter Defaults table and runtime follow-ups (probe logprobs non-null; confirm cached_tokens>0).\",\n  \"answer\": \"# Implementation-Ready Spec — Label-Free FDR Gate at the Text-to-Logic Admission Boundary\\n\\n> **Scope.** This is a copy-pasteable specification sheet for every scalar input and procedure of the\\n> decoy-competition FDR gate used to admit LLM-extracted facts/bridges into the symbolic (Prolog) layer.\\n> Every equation is quoted verbatim from a primary source with its equation number, every symbol is\\n> glossed, and each component is reduced to a language-agnostic pseudo-procedure with a recommended default.\\n> A method-executor reading **only this file** can code Phase-0 + the CLUTRR calibration diagonal with no\\n> further literature lookup. Citations `[n]` index the Sources section at the end.\\n>\\n> **Conventions used throughout.** `a ∨ b = max(a,b)`. \\\"Admission\\\" = a candidate (extracted atomic fact or\\n> multi-hop bridge) is accepted into the symbolic layer. `W_i` is the per-candidate **competition statistic**\\n> (real-candidate score minus its matched decoy score, sign-antisymmetric). `t` is the operative admission\\n> cutoff on `W`. `α` is the target FDR. The gate decides admission **by decoy competition (knockoff+)**, and\\n> uses **entrapment** as an *independent* corroborating upper bound.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## A. knockoff+/TDC thresholding and the `+1` / `1/k` minimum-estimable-FDR floor\\n\\n### A.1 The competition statistic and its required properties (verbatim)\\n\\nBarber & Candès define the statistic `W_j` and require two properties [1]:\\n\\n- **Antisymmetry property (Definition 4)** [1]: *\\\"The statistic W is said to obey the antisymmetry\\n  property if swapping X_j and X̃_j has the effect of switching the sign of W_j.\\\"* Formally, for any\\n  `S ⊆ {1,…,p}`, `W_j([X X̃]_swap(S), y) = W_j([X X̃], y) · (+1 if j∉S, −1 if j∈S)`.\\n- **Sufficiency property (Definition 3)** [1]: `W` depends on the data only through `[X X̃]ᵀ[X X̃]` and `[X X̃]ᵀy`.\\n\\nA large **positive** `W_j` is evidence the candidate is a true signal; the sign of `W_j` is the \\\"win/lose\\\"\\nof real vs. decoy.\\n\\n### A.2 The two thresholds (verbatim)\\n\\n- **knockoff (Definition 1, eq. 1.8)** [1] — controls the *modified* FDR:\\n  ```\\n  T = min { t ∈ W : #{j : W_j ≤ −t} / (#{j : W_j ≥ t} ∨ 1) ≤ q }\\n  ```\\n- **knockoff+ (Definition 2, eq. 1.9)** [1] — controls the FDR **exactly**:\\n  ```\\n  T = min { t ∈ W : ( 1 + #{j : W_j ≤ −t} ) / (#{j : W_j ≥ t} ∨ 1) ≤ q }\\n  ```\\n  Selected/admitted set: `Ŝ = { j : W_j ≥ T }` (Definition 1) [1].\\n\\n**Which controls what (verbatim theorems)** [1]:\\n- **Theorem 1 (knockoff → modified FDR):** `E[ #{j: β_j=0 and j∈Ŝ} / (#{j: j∈Ŝ} + q⁻¹) ] ≤ q`. The\\n  `q⁻¹` in the denominator makes this \\\"very close to the FDR when a high number of variables are selected,\\n  but may be quite different when a small number of variables is selected\\\" [1].\\n- **Theorem 2 (knockoff+ → FDR):** `FDR = E[ #{j: β_j=0 and j∈Ŝ} / (#{j: j∈Ŝ} ∨ 1) ] ≤ q`.\\n\\n> **Gate mapping (use knockoff+).** estimated FDR at cutoff `t`:\\n> `FDR_hat(t) = (1 + #{i : W_i ≤ −t}) / (#{i : W_i ≥ t} ∨ 1)`; admit `{i : W_i ≥ t}` at the **smallest** `t`\\n> (most permissive) with `FDR_hat(t) ≤ α`. This is exactly eq. 1.9 with `q := α`.\\n\\n### A.3 Minimum-estimable-FDR floor (`1/k`) — DERIVED, with the demonstrable-α grid\\n\\nThe numerator of eq. 1.9 is `1 + #{W_i ≤ −t} ≥ 1`; the denominator is at most `k = #admitted`. Hence the\\n**smallest attainable estimate with k admissions is `(1+0)/k = 1/k`** (achieved when zero decoy wins lie above\\n`t`). To certify `FDR_hat ≤ α` you therefore need `1/k ≤ α`, i.e. **`k ≥ ⌈1/α⌉`**. This is a hard structural\\nfloor and dictates how many admissions each anchor/relation must yield before an α is even demonstrable:\\n\\n| α | k-floor = ⌈1/α⌉ | interpretation |\\n|------|-----------------|-----------------------------------------------|\\n| 0.05 | **20** | need ≥20 admitted candidates to certify FDR≤5% |\\n| 0.10 | **10** | ≥10 admissions |\\n| 0.20 | **5**  | ≥5 admissions |\\n| 0.30 | **4**  | (1/0.3=3.33 → 4) |\\n| 0.50 | **2**  | ≥2 admissions |\\n\\n**Recommended demonstrable-α grid:** `{0.05, 0.10, 0.20, 0.30, 0.50}` — each grid point tied to its k-floor\\nabove. Phase-0/CLUTRR must guarantee per-(facts | bridges)-per-anchor admission counts ≥ the k-floor of the\\nsmallest α you intend to demonstrate, else that α is structurally unreachable regardless of model quality.\\n\\n### A.4 Is the `+1` droppable? (Rajchert & Keich, verbatim findings)\\n\\nRajchert & Keich study the general additive constant `t` in `SSSt+` (eq. 2–3 of [2], the sequential/TDC form\\nof the `+1`) and answer **the `+1` is, in general, necessary** [2]:\\n\\n- **Theorem 1 + Corollary 1** [2]: writing `((1−c)/c)·α = a/b` with `a,b` coprime, for any `t ∈ (1 − 1/b, 1]`\\n  the threshold is **unchanged** (`K_t = K_1`). So you *can* shrink the constant below 1 in some cases, **but\\n  it makes no difference to the discovery list** — no power is gained.\\n- **Theorem 2 + Corollary 2** [2]: for the `a=1` case (i.e. `α = 1/b` form, `c=1/2`), **`t = 1` is optimal**:\\n  any `t<1` either gives `K_t = K_1` or **fails to control the FDR** (they construct an explicit counterexample\\n  where `FDR(SSSt+) > α`, confirmed to bite even for moderate `n`, their Fig. 1). The result \\\"applies to TDC\\\".\\n\\n> **Spec consequence.** Do **not** drop or relax the `+1` for the headline certificate — keep eq. 1.9 as\\n> written. The conservativeness the `+1` induces is exactly the `1/k` floor of A.3; it is large only at small\\n> `k`. Any \\\"leftover-budget +1-floor relaxation\\\" experiment is **exploratory** and must be validated\\n> empirically (it has no finite-sample guarantee per Theorem 2 of [2]).\\n\\n### A.5 Leftover-budget tightening: TDC-SB / TDC-UB (Ebadi et al.) — NOT the headline\\n\\nEbadi et al. give **upper prediction bounds on the FDP** (not just its average) for competition-based FDR\\ncontrol: **TDC-SB** (standardized band) and **TDC-UB** (uniform band) [3]. They bound the decoy-win counting\\nprocess `U_d` whose marginal is **negative-binomial `NB(d, R)`**, and require a horizon parameter `d_max` [3].\\nBoth are **\\\"significantly tighter than ones obtained using … Katsevich and Ramdas\\\"** (TDC-KR) [3]. Reported\\nmedian bounds (m=2000, π₀=0.5, ρ=3) [3]:\\n\\n| confidence γ | TDC-UB | TDC-SB | TDC-KR (Katsevich–Ramdas) |\\n|--------------|--------|--------|---------------------------|\\n| 0.01 | **0.087** | 0.094 | 0.243 |\\n| 0.05 | **0.079** | 0.083 | 0.189 |\\n\\nTDC-UB is generally the tightest. **Reference implementation:** R package `bandsfdp`; the function\\n`tdc_ub(thresholds, labels, alpha, gamma, c=0.5, lambda=0.5, n=length(labels), interpolate=TRUE)` \\\"computes an\\nupper prediction bound, derived from the uniform band, on the FDP in TDC's list of discoveries\\\"; `gamma` is the\\nconfidence parameter (typical `0.05` or `0.01`), `c=0.5` sets winning target ranks for single-decoy TDC [4].\\nThe method-executor can port `bandsfdp` (tdc_ub/tdc_sb) to Python. **Mark as leftover-budget FDX tightening,\\nnot the primary certificate.**\\n\\n### A.6 Pseudo-procedure — `knockoff_plus_threshold`\\n\\n```\\nfunction knockoff_plus_threshold(W[], alpha):           # W = competition statistics (signed), one per candidate\\n    cand_cutoffs = sort( unique( |W_i| for all i ) )     # scan candidate t over distinct |W| magnitudes, ascending\\n    best = (t=+inf, admitted={}, fdr=1.0)\\n    for t in cand_cutoffs:                                # ascending t = most→least permissive as t grows\\n        pos = count(i : W_i >=  t)                        # real wins at/above t  (= #admitted at this t)\\n        neg = count(i : W_i <= -t)                        # decoy wins at/below -t\\n        fdr_hat = (1 + neg) / max(1, pos)                 # eq. 1.9\\n        if fdr_hat <= alpha:                              # feasible cutoff\\n            return (t, {i : W_i >= t}, fdr_hat)           # smallest such t = most permissive admission\\n    return (+inf, {}, 1.0)                                # no feasible cutoff: admit nothing\\n# Floor check: if max attainable #admitted < ceil(1/alpha), this alpha is structurally undemonstrable (A.3).\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## B. Valid entrapment combined/paired estimator and the ratio `r`\\n\\n**Role in the gate.** Decoy competition (Sub-task A) decides **admission**. Entrapment provides an\\n**independent, construction-distinct upper bound** on the realized FDP, compared against gold on a labeled\\nslice. Use the **combined** estimator as the default certificate and **paired** (r=1) as the tighter\\ncertificate; **never** use *sample*; use *lower bound* only to demonstrate *failure*.\\n\\nSymbols (verbatim from [5]): `N_T`, `N_E` = number of original-**target** and **entrapment** discoveries at\\nthe operative cutoff; `r` = **effective ratio of the entrapment to original target database size**\\n(`r = #entrapment / #target`, the *database-size* ratio — distinct from the discovery counts `N_T, N_E`) [5,6].\\n\\n### B.1 The four estimators (verbatim, with equation numbers from the Nature Methods paper)\\n\\n- **Lower bound (eq. 2)** [5]: `FDP̂_{T∪E} = N_E / (N_T + N_E)`.\\n  *\\\"without the 1/r term and assuming that any entrapment discovery is indeed false, equation (2) represents a\\n  lower bound on the FDP. As such, this method can only be used to indicate that a tool **fails** to control\\n  the FDR … rather than as evidence of FDR control.\\\"* [5]\\n- **Combined (eq. 1) — DEFAULT certificate** [5]:\\n  ```\\n  FDP̂_{T∪E} = N_E · (1 + 1/r) / (N_T + N_E)\\n  ```\\n  Grouping is **`(1 + 1/r)`** (verified verbatim) [5]. *\\\"under an assumption analogous to the equal-chance\\n  assumption that TDC relies on, equation (1) provides an estimated **upper bound**, that is, on average it\\n  overestimates the true FDP.\\\"* With `r = 1` it reduces to Elias & Gygi's concatenated target+decoy FDR\\n  estimate [5].\\n- **Sample (eq. 3) — INVALID, do not use** [5]:\\n  ```\\n  FDP̂_T = N_E · (1/r) / N_T          # estimates FDP only among the original-target (T) discoveries\\n  ```\\n  *\\\"the sample-entrapment method is inherently flawed because, while **typically underestimating** the FDP, it\\n  can also **overestimate** it in some unusual cases … cannot be used to provide empirical evidence that a tool\\n  controls the FDR nor that the tool fails to control the FDR.\\\"* [5]\\n- **Paired (eq. 4) — TIGHTER certificate, requires `r = 1`** [5]:\\n  ```\\n  FDP̂*_{T∪E} = ( N_E + N_{E≥s>T} + 2·N_{E>T≥s} ) / (N_T + N_E)\\n  ```\\n  where `s` = discovery cutoff score; `N_{E≥s>T}` = # discovered entrapment items (score ≥ s) whose **paired**\\n  target scores `< s`; `N_{E>T≥s}` = # discovered entrapment items whose paired target scored lower **but was\\n  still also discovered** [5]. Requires each target paired with a **unique** entrapment (so `r = 1`); a\\n  `k`-matched generalization uses `r = k`. Both are valid upper bounds \\\"in the same averaged sense\\\" as combined [5].\\n  *Tightest case is `r = 1` paired.* (OmniNovo applies exactly this `r=1` one-to-one paired entrapment \\\"following\\n  the framework proposed by Wen et al.\\\" [7].)\\n\\n### B.2 Why \\\"sample\\\" is biased (the paper's exact argument)\\n\\nThe sample method estimates the FDP **only among the original-target list `T`** (denominator `N_T`, eq. 3),\\ni.e. it targets the wrong discovery list and ignores that the relevant search space is the **augmented** T∪E\\nlist. The paper proves (Supplementary Note 3) it is **inherently flawed**: it **typically underestimates** FDP\\n(so it would falsely \\\"pass\\\" a leaky pipeline) but can also **overestimate** in unusual cases — therefore it can\\nbe used as evidence **neither** of control **nor** of failure [5].\\n\\n### B.3 How `r` propagates (point estimate, variance, achievable-α floor)\\n\\n1. **Point estimate:** `r` enters combined via the multiplicative `(1 + 1/r)` inflation. As `r → ∞`,\\n   `(1+1/r) → 1` and combined → lower bound (the difference is exactly `1/r`; the paper notes at `r = 5` the\\n   gap is `1/r = 20%`) [5]. Smaller `r` ⇒ larger inflation ⇒ more conservative upper bound.\\n2. **Variance:** smaller `r` ⇒ fewer entrapment items ⇒ smaller-count `N_E` ⇒ **higher relative variance** of\\n   `N_E` ⇒ **wider** FDP CI. Larger `r` shrinks variance but moves you away from the actual application (you are\\n   searching a much larger DB than intended) [5].\\n3. **Achievable-α floor:** an entrapment certificate cannot certify FDP below roughly its own counting\\n   granularity (≈ `1/(N_T+N_E)`); with few entrapment discoveries the smallest *credibly distinguishable* FDP\\n   is coarse. (This parallels the `1/k` floor of A.3.)\\n\\n> **Recommended default: `r = 1`, paired estimator** (tightest valid certificate; matches the hypothesis's\\n> \\\"entrapment-at-one-item\\\"). Trade-off of `r > 1`: lower variance but a looser, less application-faithful bound\\n> and `k`-matched bookkeeping. Use **combined** when pairing is unavailable.\\n\\n### B.4 Pseudo-procedure — `entrapment_fdp`\\n\\n```\\nfunction entrapment_fdp(N_T, N_E, r, estimator, paired_counts=None):\\n    if estimator == \\\"lower\\\":     return N_E / max(1, N_T + N_E)                      # eq.2  (lower bound)\\n    if estimator == \\\"combined\\\":  return N_E * (1 + 1.0/r) / max(1, N_T + N_E)        # eq.1  (default upper bound)\\n    if estimator == \\\"sample\\\":    raise Error(\\\"invalid — do not use (eq.3 is biased)\\\")\\n    if estimator == \\\"paired\\\":    # requires r==1 and per-target paired entrapment scores; s = operative cutoff\\n        N_Egt = paired_counts.E_ge_s_gt_T      # entrapment >= s whose paired target < s\\n        N_Egtt = paired_counts.E_gt_T_ge_s     # entrapment whose paired target scored lower but is also discovered\\n        return (N_E + N_Egt + 2*N_Egtt) / max(1, N_T + N_E)                          # eq.4  (tighter upper bound)\\n# Construction-independence: build entrapment by a mechanism DISTINCT from the admission decoys, so the two\\n# FDR signals (knockoff+ admission vs. entrapment bound) are independent corroborations against gold.\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## C. Document-block (cluster) bootstrap for all FDP/FDR confidence intervals\\n\\n### C.1 Threat addressed\\n\\nLLM scoring noise is **correlated within a document** (shared context, entities, genre). Treating per-candidate\\n`W` signs as i.i.d. across the pooled corpus **understates variance** and the floor — i.e. it is\\n**anti-conservative**. The fix is to resample **whole documents** (clusters/blocks), preserving within-document\\ndependence. This is the standard cluster/block-bootstrap remedy for within-group dependence: the **pairs\\ncluster bootstrap** and **wild cluster bootstrap** of Cameron, Gelbach & Miller (RESTAT 2008, 90(3):414–427),\\nwhich correct over-rejection when errors are clustered [8]; lineage also includes the moving/block bootstrap\\nfor dependent data (Künsch 1989). Resample at the **document** level, not the candidate level.\\n\\n### C.2 Procedure (concrete)\\n\\n```\\nfor b in 1..B:\\n    docs_b   = sample WITH REPLACEMENT from {documents}      # block = whole document, preserves within-doc dependence\\n    corpus_b = concat(all candidate records of docs in docs_b)\\n    t_b, S_b, fdr_b = knockoff_plus_threshold(W of corpus_b, alpha)   # re-run the WHOLE gate on the resample\\n    ent_b   = entrapment_fdp(N_T(corpus_b), N_E(corpus_b), r, estimator)   # and the entrapment bound\\n    stat_b  = realized_FDP_statistic(corpus_b)               # whatever statistic the disconfirmation tests\\ncollect {stat_b}; report percentile CI (2.5%, 97.5%).\\n# Primary disconfirmation: does the CI lie ENTIRELY on the anti-conservative (above-alpha) side?\\n```\\n\\n- **Recommended `B ≥ 2000`** (percentile-CI tail stability; `B=2000` gives stable 2.5/97.5 quantiles).\\n- **Statistic of interest** = realized FDP vs. the operative `α`; the CI used by the **primary\\n  disconfirmation** is this document-block percentile CI.\\n\\n### C.3 Two granularities — do not conflate\\n\\n- **FDP bootstrap** (above): resample **documents with replacement**, recompute the gate, get an FDP/FDR CI.\\n- **Cross-validation for S5** (leave-one-cluster-out / leave-one-document-out): a **separate** generalization\\n  check — partition documents, hold one out, evaluate. It is **not** the FDP CI and must not be mixed into the\\n  bootstrap loop.\\n\\n### C.4 Pseudo-procedure — `doc_block_bootstrap`\\n\\n```\\nfunction doc_block_bootstrap(per_doc_records, statistic_fn, B=2000):\\n    stats = []\\n    D = number of documents\\n    for b in 1..B:\\n        idx   = sample D document-indices WITH replacement\\n        boot  = concat(per_doc_records[i] for i in idx)\\n        stats.append( statistic_fn(boot) )\\n    point = statistic_fn(per_doc_records)                    # plug-in point estimate on full data\\n    return (point, percentile(stats, 2.5), percentile(stats, 97.5))\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## D. Null sign-flip property + two LLM failure modes + isolated-vs-batched discriminator\\n\\n### D.1 The sole validity condition (verbatim)\\n\\nBarber & Candès, **Lemma 1 (i.i.d. signs for the nulls)** [1]:\\n> *\\\"Let ε ∈ {±1}ᵖ be a sign sequence independent of W, with ε_j = +1 for all nonnull j and ε_j ~iid {±1} for\\n> null j. Then (W₁,…,W_p) =d (W₁·ε₁,…,W_p·ε_p).\\\"*\\n\\ni.e. **for genuinely-false (null) candidates the sign of `W_i` is an independent fair coin (P=0.5), independent\\nof `|W_i|` and of the signs of the true candidates** [1]. Consequence (eq. 1.10) [1]:\\n`#{j: β_j=0 and W_j ≥ t} =d #{j: β_j=0 and W_j ≤ −t}`, which is what makes `#{W_i ≤ −t}` a valid estimate of the\\nfalse admissions above `t`. The **TDC \\\"equal-chance\\\" assumption** [5] is the same statement in competition\\nlanguage: *a false real candidate and its matched decoy are exchangeable in the high-score tail* (each equally\\nlikely to win).\\n\\n> **Honesty caveat (state in the paper).** For LLM decoys there is **no construction-level proof** of Lemma 1\\n> (unlike Gaussian knockoffs). The gate is therefore an **empirically-validated calibration**, not a theorem;\\n> D.4 diagnostics must show the fair-coin property *holds in the tail* on labeled data.\\n\\n### D.2 Two anti-conservative failure channels (reproduce this table)\\n\\n| # | Failure channel | Mechanism | Effect on FDP | Mitigation |\\n|---|-----------------|-----------|---------------|------------|\\n| 1 | **Within-document score correlation** | Null `W` signs dependent within a document → variance/floor understated | Floor/CI too tight (anti-conservative) | **Document-block bootstrap** (Sub-task C) |\\n| 2 | **Batched-scoring contrast effects** | Model implicitly detects the fabricated/odd item among co-presented candidates and depresses decoy scores → decoys lose \\\"too often\\\" | FDP **optimistically** low (anti-conservative) | **ISOLATED, provenance-blinded, order-randomized** scoring as default |\\n\\n### D.3 Isolated-vs-batched discriminator (pre-registered test)\\n\\n```\\nRun a LABELED slice under BOTH scoring regimes:\\n  - ISOLATED : each candidate scored in its own call, provenance hidden, order randomized\\n  - BATCHED  : candidates co-presented in one call\\nDecision:\\n  if ISOLATED restores the FDR-vs-alpha diagonal (calibrated) but BATCHED is anti-conservative\\n        -> the anti-conservatism was a SCORING ARTIFACT (contrast effect); isolated scoring fixes it.\\n  if anti-conservatism PERSISTS under ISOLATED\\n        -> genuine decoy NON-exchangeability (decoys are \\\"too easy\\\"); fix the decoy family (Sub-task E).\\n```\\n**Default = isolated scoring for 100% of the confirmatory set.** Headroom is bought by **prompt caching of the\\ndocument prefix**, *not* by batching (batching reintroduces channel #2).\\n\\n### D.4 Tail diagnostics (measurement only — NEVER consumed by the gate)\\n\\n1. **Tail-conditioned win-rate** of matched (real-false, decoy) pairs **above the admission cutoff `t`** should\\n   be ≈ 0.5 (the fair-coin check of D.1).\\n2. **Upper-tail two-sample CDF test** on real-false vs. decoy scores restricted to the admission region\\n   (`scores ≥ t`): recommended **one-sided two-sample Kolmogorov–Smirnov** (or a tail-restricted Mann–Whitney\\n   U) testing whether decoy scores are stochastically *smaller* than real-false scores in the tail (which would\\n   signal non-exchangeability). \\\"Tail\\\" is delimited by `scores ≥ operative knockoff+ cutoff t`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## E. Plausibility / property-matched decoy generation\\n\\n### E.1 The load-bearing principle (DeepCoy, verbatim cautionary evidence)\\n\\nDeepCoy [9] generates **property-matched** decoys: decoys must **reproduce the property/score distribution of\\nthe true positives** and must **not be \\\"too easy.\\\"** Too-easy/biased decoys let the scorer separate on\\nartifacts and make the estimated FDR **optimistic**. Quantified by **DOE (Deviation from Optimal Embedding):**\\nDeepCoy improves DOE by an average of **81% (0.166 → 0.032 on DUD-E)** and **66% (0.109 → 0.038 on DEKOIS\\n2.0)** while \\\"introducing no discernible additional risk of false negatives\\\" [9].\\n\\n> **Text translation.** An LLM decoy must reproduce the **score distribution of genuine plausible\\n> hallucinations** — same entity types, surface form, specificity — so the *only* feature distinguishing it\\n> from a real-but-false fact is document non-entailment.\\n\\n### E.2 Primary decoy family — document-conditioned counterfactuals (+ negative control)\\n\\n- **PRIMARY: document-conditioned counterfactual decoys** — maximally-plausible, document-**non-entailed**\\n  facts/bridges drawn from the model's own prior **conditioned on the document**. Generation recipe (prompt\\n  sketch): *\\\"Given DOCUMENT and the relation/entity-type schema R(·,·), produce a fact `R(a,b)` that is\\n  plausible for this genre and these entities but **is NOT stated or entailed by the document**; match the\\n  surface form and specificity of the document's real facts.\\\"* Predicted tail-win-rate ≈ 0.5.\\n- **NEGATIVE CONTROL (keep, expect anti-conservative): random type-matched swaps** — replace an argument with a\\n  random type-matched entity. Deliberately retained as the baseline that *should* read anti-conservative\\n  (decoys too easy → optimistic FDR), validating the diagnostic.\\n\\n### E.3 Non-entailment verification gate (every decoy must pass)\\n\\nAn **accidentally-entailed** decoy is actually true → would bias the FDR **conservatively**. So every decoy\\npasses an **independent entailment check** against the document: NLI-style, or a **separate isolated LLM call**\\nasking *\\\"Is this statement entailed by the text? yes/no.\\\"* Reject (regenerate) if entailed. **Report the\\ncontamination rate** and run a **contamination sensitivity analysis** (sweep the rejection threshold).\\n*\\\"Plausibility-matched\\\"* is defined as: decoy and real share entity types / surface form / specificity, so the\\nonly difference is entailment.\\n\\n### E.4 Pseudo-procedures\\n\\n```\\nfunction generate_decoy(document, candidate_real):\\n    schema = relation_and_type_schema(candidate_real)\\n    decoy  = LLM(\\\"plausible, type/surface/specificity-matched fact under {schema} \\\"\\n                 \\\"that is NOT entailed by:\\\\n{document}\\\")\\n    return decoy\\n\\nfunction verify_non_entailment(document, decoy):           # independent, isolated call (or NLI model)\\n    return LLM_isolated(\\\"Is '{decoy}' entailed by the text? Answer yes/no.\\\\n{document}\\\") == \\\"no\\\"\\n# Accept decoy only if verify_non_entailment is True; log contamination_rate = #entailed / #generated.\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## F. Upper-tail label-free score elicitation — ranked shortlist\\n\\nGoal: a per-candidate score whose **upper tail** discriminates true from false (the admission region). Tail\\ncalibration matters far more than average calibration here.\\n\\n### F.1 Candidates with reported tail behavior\\n\\n1. **Verbalized confidence** (model states 0–100/0–1). **Overconfident in the upper tail**: Xiong et al.\\n   (ICLR 2024) find LLMs are *overconfident* when verbalizing, \\\"potentially imitating human patterns\\\";\\n   calibration improves with scale but remains far from ideal; human-inspired prompting mitigates with\\n   diminishing returns in advanced models [10]. → use as a **floor baseline**.\\n2. **Token-logprob-derived score** (sequence/avg token logprob, or yes/no-token probability of an\\n   entailment-framed prompt). Better calibrated than verbalized for **base** models, but **degrades under\\n   RLHF**: Tian et al. (EMNLP 2023) find for RLHF LMs (ChatGPT/GPT-4/Claude) the **verbalized** confidence is\\n   *typically better calibrated than the model's conditional (log)probabilities* on TriviaQA/SciQ/TruthfulQA\\n   [11]. **Requires a model exposing logprobs** (ties to Sub-task G). DINCO confirms logit access still helps\\n   calibration when available [12].\\n3. **Self-consistency / SelfCheckGPT** (Manakul et al. 2023): sample `N` completions, score by agreement;\\n   **zero-resource, black-box, no logprobs needed**, but `N×` cost [13]. The consistency-across-generations\\n   signal is correlated with correctness [12].\\n4. **DINCO — Distractor-Normalized Coherence** (2509.25532, ICLR 2026) — **overconfidence-corrected primary\\n   candidate** [12]. Verbalize confidence independently across self-generated **distractors** (alternative\\n   claims) and **normalize by the total verbalized confidence**; an off-the-shelf NLI model down-weights\\n   distractors that don't contradict the main claim; then integrate **self-consistency** via\\n   generator–validator disagreement. Exact normalization (eq. 2) [12]:\\n   ```\\n   β(C) ≈ Σ_{c∈C} f_VC(c) ;   f_NVC(c) = f_VC(c) / β(C) ≈ f_lat(c) ;   in practice β(C) ← max(1, β(C))\\n   ```\\n   where `C` = main claim + distractors, `f_VC` = raw verbalized confidence, `f_NVC` = normalized.\\n   Reported gains: **ECE improved over the best baseline by 0.077 (TriviaQA), 0.092 (SimpleQA), 0.055\\n   (FactScore)**; correlation with passage-level FactScore +0.072 (Pearson)/+0.074 (Spearman); **DINCO at 10\\n   inference calls outperforms self-consistency at 100**; relieves confidence saturation [12].\\n5. **FactSelfCheck** (2503.17229) — **fact-level black-box** [14]. Represents output as a knowledge graph of\\n   **triples `(h, r, t)`**; computes a per-fact hallucination score `H_fact` from **factual consistency across\\n   `N` stochastic samples** (KG or text variant); zero-resource, no logprobs. **Native fact-level granularity\\n   matches the gate's per-candidate unit.** Improves hallucination *correction* by **35.5%** vs SelfCheckGPT's\\n   **10.6%** [14].\\n\\n### F.2 Ranking (by: upper-tail discrimination, zero-label feasibility, cost/logprob need, isolated-scoring fit)\\n\\n| Rank | Elicitation | Upper-tail behavior | Labels | logprobs? | Cost | Phase-0 role |\\n|------|-------------|---------------------|--------|-----------|------|--------------|\\n| 1 | **DINCO** | overconfidence-**corrected**, less saturated | none | optional (helps) | ~10 calls | **primary candidate** |\\n| 2 | **FactSelfCheck** | fact-level consistency, matches unit | none | no | `N×` | sampling option, per-fact |\\n| 3 | **Self-consistency / SelfCheckGPT** | decent, saturates | none | no | `N×` | sampling baseline |\\n| 4 | **Token-logprob / yes-no-token** | good for base, RLHF-degraded | none | **yes** | 1 call | logprob variant **iff** model exposes logprobs |\\n| 5 | **Verbalized confidence** | **overconfident** | none | no | 1 call | floor baseline |\\n\\n**Recommended Phase-0 shortlist (pilot 3–4):** verbalized (floor) + **DINCO (primary)** + a **logprob/yes-no\\ntoken** variant *iff* the chosen model exposes logprobs + a sampling option (**self-consistency or\\nFactSelfCheck-style**). **Phase-0 selection metric: tail-AUC > 0.5 with CI** on a labeled slice (AUC of\\ntrue-vs-false restricted to the admission tail), **plus isolated≈batched agreement** (D.3).\\n\\n### F.3 Coupling to Sub-task G (contingency)\\n\\nIf no affordable model exposes usable logprobs, **drop the logprob elicitation**; **DINCO + verbalized +\\nself-consistency/FactSelfCheck** carry Phase-0 (all logprob-free). The pilot is thus codeable regardless of\\nlogprob availability.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## G. OpenRouter model: logprobs + prompt caching + sub-$0.30/M pricing\\n\\n### G.1 The central tension\\n\\nCheap auto-caching models (DeepSeek, Gemini Flash tier) cache the document prefix well but expose token\\n`logprobs` unevenly through OpenRouter; the **OpenAI GPT-4.1 family** reliably exposes `logprobs`/`top_logprobs`\\n*and* auto-caches — and the **nano** tier is under the $0.30/M input cap. OpenRouter supports `logprobs` +\\n`top_logprobs` (an integer 0–20 most-likely tokens per position; `logprobs` must be `true`), available for **all\\nxAI models, the OpenAI GPT-4.1 series, and several open-weight models (5–20 logprobs)** [18].\\n\\n### G.2 Concrete model table (current OpenRouter pricing)\\n\\n| model id | input $/M | output $/M | cache-read mult. | caching | logprobs? | notes |\\n|----------|-----------|------------|------------------|---------|-----------|-------|\\n| **openai/gpt-4.1-nano** | **$0.10** [16] | $0.40 [16] | 0.25–0.5× (writes free) [15] | auto (implicit) | **yes** (GPT-4.1 series) [18] | **PRIMARY** — cheapest with logprobs+caching |\\n| openai/gpt-4o-mini | $0.15 [17] | $0.60 [17] | 0.5× (writes free) [15] | auto | **yes** [18] | fallback 1 (more capable) |\\n| openai/gpt-4.1-mini | $0.40 [17] | $1.60 [17] | 0.25–0.5× | auto | yes [18] | **EXCEEDS $0.30 input cap** — excluded |\\n| deepseek (V3 tier) | sub-$0.30 (verify) | — | implicit/auto [15] | auto | **uneven via OR** | fallback 2 (**logprob-free** path) |\\n| google/gemini-flash-lite tier | sub-$0.30 (verify) | — | implicit caching [15] | auto | uneven | logprob-free path |\\n\\n`[15]` = OpenRouter prompt-caching doc. Cache-read multipliers per provider [15]: **OpenAI** writes free /\\nreads **0.25× or 0.5×**; **Grok (xAI)** reads 0.25×; **Moonshot** reads 0.25×; **Groq** reads 0.5×; **Alibaba\\nQwen** writes **1.25×** / reads **0.1×** (needs explicit `cache_control:{\\\"type\\\":\\\"ephemeral\\\"}`, 5-min TTL);\\n**Anthropic** needs explicit `cache_control` breakpoints, negative discount on writes (≈1.25×) / positive on\\nreads (≈0.1×); **DeepSeek & Gemini 2.5** = implicit/automatic. Cache hits are verifiable via\\n`usage.prompt_tokens_details.cached_tokens` (and `cache_write_tokens`) on every response [15].\\n\\n### G.3 Budget arithmetic (validated against the hard cap)\\n\\nWorkload ≈ **14.4K isolated scoring calls + ~0.7K generation calls + pilot ≈ 15.1K calls**, ~**450 input +\\n~30 output tokens/call** ⇒ ~**6.8M input + ~0.45M output** (≈7M; upper-bound design ~15M).\\n\\n- **gpt-4.1-nano** (no caching): `6.8M×$0.10/M + 0.45M×$0.40/M = $0.68 + $0.18 = $0.86`. With document-prefix\\n  caching (≈400 of 450 input tokens cached at 0.25–0.5×): input → ~$0.30–0.45 ⇒ **≈ $0.5–0.7**.\\n- **gpt-4.1-nano** (15M upper-bound, ~14M in/1M out): `$1.40 + $0.40 = $1.80` uncached → **≈ $1.0–1.5** cached.\\n- **gpt-4o-mini** (15M): `14M×$0.15 + 1M×$0.60 = $2.10 + $0.60 = $2.70` uncached → **≈ $1.5–2.5** cached.\\n\\nAll land in the **~$1–3 zone, well under the $10 hard cap** [15,16,17].\\n\\n### G.4 Recommendation\\n\\n- **PRIMARY: `openai/gpt-4.1-nano`** ($0.10/$0.40, logprobs ✓, auto-cache) — enables **all** Sub-task F\\n  elicitations including the **logprob/yes-no-token** variant.\\n- **FALLBACK 1: `openai/gpt-4o-mini`** ($0.15/$0.60, logprobs ✓) — same capabilities, more headroom/quality.\\n- **FALLBACK 2 (logprob-free): a cheap auto-caching model (DeepSeek V3 / Gemini Flash-Lite tier)** — run\\n  **DINCO + verbalized + self-consistency/FactSelfCheck** (F.3) so the pipeline is never blocked if logprobs are\\n  unavailable.\\n- **Runtime gate (follow-up):** the method-executor must **probe logprobs return non-null on a 1-call test**\\n  and **confirm `cached_tokens > 0`** before committing the budget. If the probe fails on nano, fall to the\\n  logprob-free path on Fallback 2.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## H. Novelty-positioning note\\n\\nA targeted sweep finds **no prior work that applies knockoff / target-decoy / entrapment competition FDR control\\nat an LLM neuro-symbolic (text-to-logic) admission boundary, label-free.** The nearest families all (a) require\\n**labeled** calibration data and/or (b) certify the **output**, not the **admission** of intermediate\\nfacts/bridges into a symbolic layer:\\n\\n- **Conformal factuality** (Mohri & Hashimoto, ICML 2024, arXiv 2402.10978): splits LLM output into atomic\\n  sub-claims and filters those below a conformal factuality threshold for a marginal correctness guarantee —\\n  but the threshold is set on a **labeled calibration set** and it certifies the **emitted answer** [19].\\n- **Coherent factuality** (arXiv 2505.17126) extends this to reasoning chains — still conformal/labeled [21].\\n- **Conformal selection / Selection by Prediction with Conformal p-values** (Jin & Candès, JMLR 2023, arXiv\\n  2210.01408): wraps any predictor to select candidates while controlling FDR — but needs **labeled\\n  calibration outcomes** [20].\\n- Conformal-Labeling / risk-controlling extraction for clinical entities (e.g. arXiv 2603.00924): FDR/RCPS\\n  guarantees, again **conformal (labeled)**.\\n- LINC / Logic-LM and ontology-constraint filtering (ODKE+/SHACL): symbolic-side filtering, not a statistical\\n  FDR knob and not decoy-based.\\n\\n**Near-miss to report (not a pre-emption):** *\\\"Neuro-Symbolic Verification for Preventing LLM Hallucinations in\\nProcess Control\\\"* (MDPI Processes 2024) uses **Abductive Logic Programming coherence + counter-abduction** to\\nscore LLM explanations [22] — same neuro-symbolic-anti-hallucination *spirit* but a **logic-coherence** method,\\n**not** decoy-competition FDR and **not** an admission-boundary FDR knob.\\n\\n**Differentiator (one line for the paper):** *ours is the first to convert the proteomics target-decoy/knockoff\\ncompetition machinery into a **label-free**, finite-sample FDR knob that gates the **text→logic admission\\nboundary**, using **counterfactual decoys** as the negative control in place of a labeled calibration set.*\\nConfirmatory searches (\\\"knockoff filter LLM hallucination\\\", \\\"target-decoy competition language model fact\\nextraction\\\", \\\"FDR control neuro-symbolic admission\\\") surfaced only proteomics TDC/knockoff work and conformal\\n(labeled) LLM methods — **no 2025–2026 preprint pre-empts the claim.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Parameter Defaults table (recommended values + justification)\\n\\n| Parameter | Default | Justification / source |\\n|-----------|---------|------------------------|\\n| **α grid** | `{0.05, 0.10, 0.20, 0.30, 0.50}` | each tied to k-floor `⌈1/α⌉` = {20,10,5,4,2} (A.3) |\\n| **FDR estimator (admission)** | knockoff+ eq. 1.9 | exact finite-sample FDR (Thm 2 [1]); keep the `+1` (Thm 2 [2]) |\\n| **Tolerance τ (FDR-vs-α slack)** | `0.05` absolute | small slack absorbs the `1/k` granularity (A.3) without masking real anti-conservatism; report sensitivity to τ∈{0,0.05} |\\n| **N_false_min** | `40` | from hypothesis; ensures ≥ k-floor for the demonstrable α grid and stable tail diagnostics |\\n| **Entrapment ratio r** | `1` (paired, eq. 4) | tightest valid upper bound; matches r=1 one-to-one pairing [5,7]; combined (eq. 1) when pairing unavailable |\\n| **Entrapment estimator** | paired (default), combined (fallback) | both valid upper bounds [5]; never `sample` (eq. 3, invalid) |\\n| **Bootstrap B** | `≥ 2000` | stable 2.5/97.5 percentile CI; document-block resampling (C) |\\n| **Bootstrap unit** | whole document (cluster) | within-doc score dependence → cluster bootstrap [8] |\\n| **Self-consistency N** (if used) | `5–10` | DINCO @10 calls > self-consistency @100 [12]; start at 10, drop if cost-bound |\\n| **Tail cutoff** | `= operative knockoff+ t` | \\\"tail\\\" = admission region `W ≥ t` (D.4) |\\n| **Scoring regime** | isolated, provenance-blinded, order-randomized | avoids batched contrast effect (D.2 channel #2); caching buys headroom |\\n| **Decoy family** | document-conditioned counterfactual + non-entailment gate | property-matched principle (DeepCoy [9]); random swap = negative control |\\n| **Tail tests** | one-sided KS (+ tail Mann–Whitney) on `W ≥ t` | exchangeability diagnostics, measurement-only (D.4) |\\n| **Primary model** | `openai/gpt-4.1-nano` | $0.10/$0.40, logprobs+caching, <$0.30 input [16,18]; fallbacks gpt-4o-mini, then logprob-free DeepSeek/Gemini |\\n| **Budget** | ≈ $1–3 (hard A label-free\nconfidence elicitation scores both; the knockoff+ rule turns decoy wins into an FDR\ncertificate. ANALYSES: S1 decoy signature (tail win-rate ~0.5, upper-tail KS/MW, doc-block\n     bootstrap); spontaneous-error tail match (decoy ~ spont, decoy != truepos);\n     G!=S ablation (4 configs); method-vs-baseline realized-FDR calibration; BH.\n\nUsage:\n  uv run method.py --selftest          # offline stat unit tests, no API\n  uv run method.py --mini              # 3-doc smoke (mini_data_out.json)\n  uv run method.py --n-docs 40         # first 40 docs, headline only\n  uv run method.py --n-docs 40 --ablation\n  uv run method.py                     # full: all docs headline + ablation on pilot\n\"\"\"\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport argparse\nimport asyncio\nimport gc\nimport json\nimport math\nimport random\nimport resource\nimport sys\nimport time\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nimport numpy as np\nfrom loguru import logger\n\nimport fdr_stats as st\nfrom llm_client import (OpenRouterClient, BudgetExceeded, parse_yes_conf,\n                        yes_prob_from_logprobs)\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Constants / guardrails\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nHERE = Path(__file__).resolve().parent\nDEP_DATA = Path(\"/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_MQN7mBg4AhvH/3_invention_loop/\"\n                \"iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1\")\nFULL_DATA = DEP_DATA / \"full_data_out.json\"\nMINI_DATA = DEP_DATA / \"mini_data_out.json\"\n\nSEED = 20240617\nALPHA_GRID = [0.05, 0.10, 0.20, 0.30, 0.50]      # k-floors {20,10,5,4,2}\nB_BOOT = 2000\nK_SC = 5                                          # self-consistency samples (portable)\nN_FALSE_MIN = 40                                  # spontaneous-error populability floor\nSOFT_CAP_USD = 1.5\nHARD_STOP_USD = 10.0\n\nPRIMARY_MODEL = \"openai/gpt-4.1-nano\"             # logprobs + cheap\nOTHER_MODEL = \"mistralai/ministral-8b-2512\"       # cross-family, cheap ($0.15/M), no logprobs\n\nlogger.remove()\nlogger.add(sys.stdout, level=\"INFO\", format=\"{time:HH:mm:ss}|{level:<7}|{message}\")\n(HERE / \"logs\").mkdir(exist_ok=True)\nlogger.add(HERE / \"logs\" / \"run.log\", rotation=\"30 MB\", level=\"DEBUG\")\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Memory limit (data is tiny; cap generously to fail fast not crash)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef set_mem_limit(gb: float = 8.0):\n    try:\n        soft = int(gb * 1024**3)\n        resource.setrlimit(resource.RLIMIT_AS, (soft, soft))\n    except (ValueError, OSError) as e:\n        logger.warning(f\"could not set RLIMIT_AS: {e}\")\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Data loading + crisp gold\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef verbalize(h: str, r: str, t: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"CLUTRR triple (h, r, t) means 'tail is head's relation' => '{t} is the {r} of {h}.'\"\"\"\n    return f\"{t} is the {r} of {h}.\"\n\n\ndef _doc_seed(doc_id: str, salt: int = 0) -> int:\n    \"\"\"Stable per-document seed (hashlib, not Python's randomized hash()) so extraction\n    shuffles, decoy fallbacks, and swaps are reproducible across runs and doc subsets.\"\"\"\n    import hashlib\n    h = hashlib.sha256(f\"{doc_id}|{SEED}|{salt}\".encode()).hexdigest()\n    return int(h[:12], 16)\n\n\nclass Doc:\n    __slots__ = (\"doc_id\", \"text\", \"entities\", \"query\", \"k\", \"is_pilot\", \"fold\",\n                 \"gold_true\", \"gold_rel\", \"gold_pairs\", \"atomic_pairs\", \"multi_pairs\",\n                 \"atomic_facts\", \"multi_facts\")\n\n    def __init__(self, raw: dict):\n        inp = json.loads(raw[\"input\"])\n        out = json.loads(raw[\"output\"])\n        self.doc_id = inp[\"doc_id\"]\n        self.text = inp[\"document_text\"]\n        self.entities = [e[\"name\"] for e in inp[\"entities\"]]\n        self.query = inp.get(\"query\", {})\n        self.k = int(raw[\"metadata_chain_length_k\"])\n        self.is_pilot = bool(raw[\"metadata_is_pilot\"])\n        self.fold = raw[\"metadata_fold\"]\n        self.atomic_facts = [(f[\"head\"], f[\"relation\"], f[\"tail\"]) for f in out[\"atomic_facts\"]]\n        self.multi_facts = [(f[\"head\"], f[\"relation\"], f[\"tail\"]) for f in out[\"multi_hop_facts\"]]\n        self.gold_true = set(self.atomic_facts) | set(self.multi_facts)\n        self.gold_rel: dict[tuple[str, str], str] = {}\n        for (hh, rr, tt) in self.gold_true:\n            self.gold_rel[(hh, tt)] = rr\n        self.atomic_pairs = [(h, t) for (h, r, t) in self.atomic_facts]\n        self.multi_pairs = [(h, t) for (h, r, t) in self.multi_facts]\n        self.gold_pairs = set(self.gold_rel.keys())\n\n    def label(self, h: str, r: str, t: str) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Crisp 3-way label vs CLUTRR gold (exact).\"\"\"\n        if (h, r, t) in self.gold_true:\n            return \"TRUE\"\n        if (h, t) in self.gold_pairs and r != self.gold_rel[(h, t)]:\n            return \"FALSE\"   # contradiction on an enumerated pair\n        return \"UNDECIDABLE\"\n\n\ndef load_docs(path: Path, n_docs: int | None = None,\n              pilot_only: bool = False) -> list[Doc]:\n    raw = json.loads(path.read_text())\n    examples = raw[\"datasets\"][0][\"examples\"]\n    docs = [Doc(e) for e in examples]\n    if pilot_only:\n        docs = [d for d in docs if d.is_pilot]\n    if n_docs is not None:\n        docs = docs[:n_docs]\n    return docs\n\n\nRELATION_VOCAB = [\"aunt\", \"brother\", \"daughter\", \"daughter-in-law\", \"father\",\n                  \"father-in-law\", \"granddaughter\", \"grandfather\", \"grandmother\",\n                  \"grandson\", \"husband\", \"mother\", \"mother-in-law\", \"nephew\", \"niece\",\n                  \"sister\", \"son\", \"son-in-law\", \"uncle\", \"wife\"]\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Prompts\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef extract_messages(doc: Doc, pairs: list[tuple[str, str]]) -> list[dict]:\n    \"\"\"Task 1: free atomic extraction (sentences). Task 2: fill-in-the-blank relation for\n    each target pair, phrased EXACTLY as the scoring claim ('{tail} is the ___ of {head}')\n    so the direction convention is unambiguous and matches scoring verbalization.\"\"\"\n    vocab = \", \".join(RELATION_VOCAB)\n    stubs = \"\\n\".join(f\"{i+1}. {t} is the ___ of {h}\" for i, (h, t) in enumerate(pairs))\n    sysmsg = (\"You extract kinship facts from a short story. Use ONLY these relation \"\n              f\"words (exact spelling): {vocab}.\")\n    user = (f\"Document:\\n{doc.text}\\n\\n\"\n            f\"People: {', '.join(doc.entities)}\\n\\n\"\n            \"TASK 1 (STATED FACTS): List every kinship relationship DIRECTLY stated in the \"\n            \"text, each as one sentence of the form \\\"<Person> is the <relation> of <Person>\\\".\\n\\n\"\n            \"TASK 2 (INFERRED RELATIONS): Complete each numbered statement below with the \"\n            \"single most likely relation word from the vocabulary. The relationship may be \"\n            \"directly stated or require reasoning over the family tree. Give exactly one \"\n            \"relation per item, in order.\\n\"\n            f\"{stubs}\\n\\n\"\n            \"Respond with STRICT JSON only, no prose:\\n\"\n            \"{\\\"stated\\\": [\\\"<sentence>\\\", ...], \"\n            \"\\\"inferred\\\": [\\\"<relation_for_1>\\\", \\\"<relation_for_2>\\\", ...]}\")\n    return [{\"role\": \"system\", \"content\": sysmsg}, {\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": user}]\n\n\ndef decoy_messages(doc: Doc, items: list[tuple[str, str, str]]) -> list[dict]:\n    \"\"\"items: list of (head, current_relation, tail). Ask for plausible ALTERNATIVE\n    relations for the SAME claim '{tail} is the ___ of {head}' (counterfactual decoy).\"\"\"\n    vocab = \", \".join(RELATION_VOCAB)\n    lines = \"\\n\".join(f\"{i+1}. \\\"{t} is the {r} of {h}\\\"  (current relation: {r})\"\n                      for i, (h, r, t) in enumerate(items))\n    sysmsg = (\"You propose alternative kinship relations. Use ONLY these relation words \"\n              f\"(exact spelling): {vocab}.\")\n    user = (\"For each numbered statement below, give the TWO next most plausible \"\n            \"ALTERNATIVE relation words (each different from the current one), most \"\n            \"plausible first — a likely-but-possibly-wrong guess for that exact statement.\\n\"\n            f\"{lines}\\n\\n\"\n            \"Respond with STRICT JSON only: a JSON array with one [alt1, alt2] pair per \"\n            \"numbered item, in order: [[\\\"alt1\\\",\\\"alt2\\\"], [\\\"alt1\\\",\\\"alt2\\\"], ...]\")\n    return [{\"role\": \"system\", \"content\": sysmsg}, {\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": user}]\n\n\n_STATED_RE = None\n\n\ndef parse_stated_sentences(text: str) -> set:\n    \"\"\"Parse 'B is the R of A' sentences -> triples (A, R, B) [head=A, tail=B].\"\"\"\n    import re\n    global _STATED_RE\n    if _STATED_RE is None:\n        _STATED_RE = re.compile(r\"([A-Z][a-zA-Z]+)\\s+is\\s+the\\s+([a-zA-Z\\-]+)\\s+of\\s+([A-Z][a-zA-Z]+)\")\n    out = set()\n    for m in _STATED_RE.finditer(text or \"\"):\n        b, r, a = m.group(1), _norm_rel(m.group(2)), m.group(3)\n        if r:\n            out.add((a, r, b))\n    return out\n\n\ndef score_messages_logprob(doc_text: str, claim: str) -> list[dict]:\n    return [\n        {\"role\": \"system\", \"content\":\n            \"You check whether a kinship claim is logically entailed by the document. \"\n            \"A claim is entailed if it is directly stated OR can be derived from stated \"\n            \"facts. Answer with exactly one word: Yes or No.\"},\n        {\"role\": \"user\", \"content\":\n            f\"Document: {doc_text}\\n\\nClaim: {claim}\\n\"\n            \"Is this claim entailed by the document? Answer Yes or No.\"},\n    ]\n\n\ndef score_messages_portable(doc_text: str, claim: str) -> list[dict]:\n    return [\n        {\"role\": \"system\", \"content\":\n            \"You check whether a kinship claim is logically entailed by the document. \"\n            \"A claim is entailed if it is directly stated OR can be derived from stated facts.\"},\n        {\"role\": \"user\", \"content\":\n            f\"Document: {doc_text}\\n\\nClaim: {claim}\\n\"\n            \"Is this claim entailed by the document? Respond in EXACTLY this format:\\n\"\n            \"Answer: <Yes or No>\\nConfidence: <integer 0-100>\"},\n    ]\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# JSON parsing from LLM output\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef _extract_json(text: str | None):\n    if not text:\n        return None\n    t = text.strip()\n    if t.startswith(\"```\"):\n        t = t.strip(\"`\")\n        if t[:4].lower() == \"json\":\n            t = t[4:]\n    # find first balanced {...} or [...]\n    for opener, closer in ((\"{\", \"}\"), (\"[\", \"]\")):\n        i = t.find(opener)\n        if i == -1:\n            continue\n        depth = 0\n        for j in range(i, len(t)):\n            if t[j] == opener:\n                depth += 1\n            elif t[j] == closer:\n                depth -= 1\n                if depth == 0:\n                    try:\n                        return json.loads(t[i:j + 1])\n                    except json.JSONDecodeError:\n                        break\n    try:\n        return json.loads(t)\n    except json.JSONDecodeError:\n        return None\n\n\ndef _norm_rel(r: str) -> str | None:\n    if not isinstance(r, str):\n        return None\n    r = r.strip().lower()\n    return r if r in RELATION_VOCAB else None\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Extraction (one call per doc) -> reals (labeled) + atomic free-extraction P/R\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nasync def extract_doc(client: OpenRouterClient, doc: Doc, rng: random.Random) -> dict:\n    # all gold pairs (atomic + multi-hop), shuffled so the model can't tell type by order\n    pairs = list(doc.atomic_pairs) + list(doc.multi_pairs)\n    pair_type = {p: \"atomic\" for p in doc.atomic_pairs}\n    for p in doc.multi_pairs:\n        pair_type.setdefault(p, \"multi_hop\")\n    shuffled = pairs[:]\n    rng.shuffle(shuffled)\n    res = await client.call(PRIMARY_MODEL, extract_messages(doc, shuffled),\n                            max_tokens=900, temperature=0.0)\n    parsed = _extract_json(res[\"content\"]) or {}\n    stated = parsed.get(\"stated\") if isinstance(parsed, dict) else None\n    inferred = parsed.get(\"inferred\") if isinstance(parsed, dict) else None\n    stated = stated if isinstance(stated, list) else []\n    inferred = inferred if isinstance(inferred, list) else []\n\n    # free atomic extraction -> precision/recall vs gold atomic facts\n    stated_triples = set()\n    stated_text_parts = []\n    for s in stated:\n        if isinstance(s, str):\n            stated_text_parts.append(s)\n        elif isinstance(s, list) and len(s) == 3:  # tolerate triple form [A,rel,B]\n            h, r, t = str(s[0]).strip(), _norm_rel(s[1]), str(s[2]).strip()\n            if r:\n                stated_triples.add((h, r, t))\n    for (a, r, b) in parse_stated_sentences(\"\\n\".join(stated_text_parts)):\n        if a in doc.entities and b in doc.entities:\n            stated_triples.add((a, r, b))\n    gold_atomic = set(doc.atomic_facts)\n    tp = len(stated_triples & gold_atomic)\n    prec = tp / len(stated_triples) if stated_triples else float(\"nan\")\n    rec = tp / len(gold_atomic) if gold_atomic else float(\"nan\")\n\n    # forced per-pair predictions (positional list aligned to shuffled pairs) -> reals\n    pred_rel: dict[tuple[str, str], str] = {}\n    for idx, (h, t) in enumerate(shuffled):\n        r = _norm_rel(inferred[idx]) if idx < len(inferred) else None\n        if r:\n            pred_rel[(h, t)] = r\n    reals = []\n    n_mh_correct = n_mh_total = 0\n    for (h, t) in pairs:\n        r = pred_rel.get((h, t))\n        if r is None:\n            # model failed to predict this pair: skip (logged as miss)\n            continue\n        lab = doc.label(h, r, t)\n        ftype = pair_type[(h, t)]\n        if ftype == \"multi_hop\":\n            n_mh_total += 1\n            if r == doc.gold_rel.get((h, t)):\n                n_mh_correct += 1\n        reals.append({\n            \"cand_id\": f\"{doc.doc_id}:real:{h}>{t}\", \"doc_id\": doc.doc_id,\n            \"h\": h, \"r\": r, \"t\": t, \"fact_type\": ftype, \"label\": lab,\n            \"claim\": verbalize(h, r, t),\n        })\n    return {\n        \"doc_id\": doc.doc_id, \"reals\": reals,\n        \"atomic_prec\": prec, \"atomic_rec\": rec,\n        \"n_stated\": len(stated_triples), \"n_pairs\": len(pairs),\n        \"mh_acc\": (n_mh_correct / n_mh_total) if n_mh_total else float(\"nan\"),\n        \"n_mh\": n_mh_total,\n    }\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Decoy generation (counterfactual, batched per doc) + swap control (deterministic)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef verify_nonentailed(doc: Doc, h: str, r: str, t: str, avoid: set[str]) -> bool:\n    if r in avoid:\n        return False\n    if (h, r, t) in doc.gold_true:\n        return False\n    if (h, t) in doc.gold_pairs and r == doc.gold_rel[(h, t)]:\n        return False\n    return True\n\n\nasync def gen_counterfactual_decoys(client: OpenRouterClient, doc: Doc,\n                                    reals: list[dict], model: str,\n                                    rng: random.Random) -> tuple[list[dict], int, int]:\n    \"\"\"Return (decoys, n_generated, n_contaminated). One batched call per doc.\"\"\"\n    items = [(c[\"h\"], c[\"r\"], c[\"t\"]) for c in reals]\n    if not items:\n        return [], 0, 0\n    res = await client.call(model, decoy_messages(doc, items),\n                            max_tokens=700, temperature=0.0)\n    parsed = _extract_json(res[\"content\"])\n    decoys, n_gen, n_contam = [], 0, 0\n    for i, c in enumerate(reals):\n        h, t, r_real = c[\"h\"], c[\"t\"], c[\"r\"]\n        gold_r = doc.gold_rel.get((h, t))\n        if isinstance(parsed, list):\n            alts = parsed[i] if i < len(parsed) else None\n        elif isinstance(parsed, dict):\n            alts = parsed.get(str(i + 1))\n        else:\n            alts = None\n        cand_rels = []\n        if isinstance(alts, list):\n            for a in alts:\n                rr = _norm_rel(a)\n                if rr:\n                    n_gen += 1\n                    if rr == gold_r:\n                        n_contam += 1\n                    cand_rels.append(rr)\n        # choose first alt that is verified non-entailed and != real relation\n        avoid = {r_real}\n        chosen = None\n        for rr in cand_rels:\n            if verify_nonentailed(doc, h, rr, t, avoid):\n                chosen = rr\n                break\n        if chosen is None:\n            # deterministic fallback: a random vocab relation passing verification\n            pool = [x for x in RELATION_VOCAB if verify_nonentailed(doc, h, x, t, avoid)]\n            if pool:\n                chosen = pool[rng.randrange(len(pool))]\n        if chosen is None:\n            continue\n        decoys.append({\n            \"cand_id\": f\"{doc.doc_id}:cf:{h}>{t}\", \"doc_id\": doc.doc_id,\n            \"h\": h, \"r\": chosen, \"t\": t, \"pair\": (h, t), \"real_id\": c[\"cand_id\"],\n            \"claim\": verbalize(h, chosen, t),\n        })\n    return decoys, n_gen, n_contam\n\n\ndef gen_swaps(doc: Doc, reals: list[dict], rng: random.Random) -> list[dict]:\n    swaps = []\n    persons = list(doc.entities)\n    for c in reals:\n        h, r, t = c[\"h\"], c[\"r\"], c[\"t\"]\n        pool = [p for p in persons if p != t and p != h\n                and verify_nonentailed(doc, h, r, p, set())]\n        if not pool:\n            continue\n        tp = pool[rng.randrange(len(pool))]\n        swaps.append({\n            \"cand_id\": f\"{doc.doc_id}:swap:{h}>{t}\", \"doc_id\": doc.doc_id,\n            \"h\": h, \"r\": r, \"t\": tp, \"real_id\": c[\"cand_id\"],\n            \"claim\": verbalize(h, r, tp),\n        })\n    return swaps\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Scoring (isolated, provenance-blinded). logprob => 1 call; portable => K_SC calls.\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nasync def score_logprob(client: OpenRouterClient, model: str, doc_text: str,\n                        claim: str) -> float:\n    res = await client.call(model, score_messages_logprob(doc_text, claim),\n                            max_tokens=16, temperature=0.0, logprobs=True, top_logprobs=5)\n    z = yes_prob_from_logprobs(res[\"top_logprobs\"], res[\"content\"])\n    return float(z) if z is not None else 0.5\n\n\nasync def score_portable(client: OpenRouterClient, model: str, doc_text: str,\n                         claim: str) -> float:\n    ps = []\n    for i in range(K_SC):\n        res = await client.call(model, score_messages_portable(doc_text, claim),\n                                max_tokens=24, temperature=0.7, seed=SEED + i, sample_idx=i)\n        p = parse_yes_conf(res[\"content\"])\n        if p is not None:\n            ps.append(p)\n    return float(np.mean(ps)) if ps else 0.5\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Orchestration helpers\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nasync def run_batched(coros: list, batch: int, label: str, client: OpenRouterClient):\n    \"\"\"Run coroutines in batches, logging running cost. Returns results in order.\"\"\"\n    out = []\n    for i in range(0, len(coros), batch):\n        chunk = coros[i:i + batch]\n        res = await asyncio.gather(*chunk, return_exceptions=True)\n        for r in res:\n            if isinstance(r, BudgetExceeded):\n                raise r\n            out.append(None if isinstance(r, Exception) else r)\n        n_err = sum(1 for r in res if isinstance(r, Exception))\n        logger.info(f\"  [{label}] {min(i+batch, len(coros))}/{len(coros)} done | \"\n                    f\"cost=${client.cost_usd:.4f} | live={client.n_calls_live} \"\n                    f\"cached={client.n_calls_cached} | errs={n_err}\")\n    return out\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# MAIN PIPELINE\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nasync def run(docs: list[Doc], do_ablation: bool, cache_dir: Path, cost_log: Path,\n              concurrency: int, portable_headline: bool = False) -> dict:\n    rng = random.Random(SEED)\n    t0 = time.time()\n    async with OpenRouterClient(cache_dir, cost_log, concurrency=concurrency,\n                                soft_cap_usd=SOFT_CAP_USD,\n                                hard_stop_usd=HARD_STOP_USD) as client:\n        # ---- 1. EXTRACTION ----\n        logger.info(f\"Extraction over {len(docs)} docs...\")\n        ext = await run_batched([extract_doc(client, d, random.Random(_doc_seed(d.doc_id)))\n                                 for d in docs], 64, \"extract\", client)\n        doc_by_id = {d.doc_id: d for d in docs}\n        reals_by_doc: dict[str, list[dict]] = {}\n        ext_meta = []\n        for d, e in zip(docs, ext):\n            if e is None:\n                reals_by_doc[d.doc_id] = []\n                continue\n            reals_by_doc[d.doc_id] = e[\"reals\"]\n            ext_meta.append(e)\n        all_reals = [c for d in docs for c in reals_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n        n_spont = sum(1 for c in all_reals if c[\"label\"] == \"FALSE\")\n        n_true = sum(1 for c in all_reals if c[\"label\"] == \"TRUE\")\n        n_und = sum(1 for c in all_reals if c[\"label\"] == \"UNDECIDABLE\")\n        logger.info(f\"reals={len(all_reals)} TRUE={n_true} FALSE(spont)={n_spont} \"\n                    f\"UNDECIDABLE={n_und}\")\n\n        # ---- 2. DECOYS (nano counterfactual) + SWAPS ----\n        logger.info(\"Generating counterfactual decoys (nano) + swaps...\")\n        dec = await run_batched([gen_counterfactual_decoys(client, d, reals_by_doc[d.doc_id],\n                                 PRIMARY_MODEL, random.Random(_doc_seed(d.doc_id, 7)))\n                                 for d in docs], 64, \"decoy\", client)\n        cf_by_doc, swap_by_doc = {}, {}\n        n_gen = n_contam = 0\n        for d, dd in zip(docs, dec):\n            decoys, g, c = dd if dd else ([], 0, 0)\n            cf_by_doc[d.doc_id] = decoys\n            n_gen += g\n            n_contam += c\n            swap_by_doc[d.doc_id] = gen_swaps(d, reals_by_doc[d.doc_id],\n                                              random.Random(_doc_seed(d.doc_id, 99)))\n        contamination_rate = (n_contam / n_gen) if n_gen else 0.0\n        logger.info(f\"decoys generated; contamination_rate={contamination_rate:.4f}\")\n\n        # ---- 3. HEADLINE SCORING (nano logprob) for reals + cf + swaps ----\n        logger.info(\"Headline scoring (nano logprob)...\")\n        zmap: dict[tuple[str, str], float] = {}     # (config, cand_id) -> raw Z\n\n        def add_score_tasks(cands, config, model, elic):\n            tasks = []\n            for c in cands:\n                d = doc_by_id[c[\"doc_id\"]]\n                if elic == \"logprob\":\n                    tasks.append((\"L\", config, c[\"cand_id\"], model, d.text, c[\"claim\"]))\n                else:\n                    tasks.append((\"P\", config, c[\"cand_id\"], model, d.text, c[\"claim\"]))\n            return tasks\n\n        all_cf = [c for d in docs for c in cf_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n        all_swap = [c for d in docs for c in swap_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n\n        async def run_score(task):\n            kind, config, cid, model, dtext, claim = task\n            z = (await score_logprob(client, model, dtext, claim) if kind == \"L\"\n                 else await score_portable(client, model, dtext, claim))\n            return (config, cid, z)\n\n        headline_tasks = (add_score_tasks(all_reals, \"nano_logprob\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"logprob\")\n                          + add_score_tasks(all_cf, \"nano_logprob\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"logprob\")\n                          + add_score_tasks(all_swap, \"nano_logprob\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"logprob\"))\n        res = await run_batched([run_score(t) for t in headline_tasks], 400, \"score-head\", client)\n        for r in res:\n            if r:\n                zmap[(r[0], r[1])] = r[2]\n\n        # ---- 3b. PORTABLE HEADLINE SCORING (nano self-consistency) on ALL docs ----\n        # Gives a full-power, same-docs controlled comparison of the two elicitations and\n        # certified admissions at strict alpha (the pilot-only portable slice is underpowered).\n        if portable_headline:\n            logger.info(f\"Portable headline scoring (nano self-consistency, K={K_SC})...\")\n            ptasks = (add_score_tasks(all_reals, \"nano_portable\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"portable\")\n                      + add_score_tasks(all_cf, \"nano_portable\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"portable\")\n                      + add_score_tasks(all_swap, \"nano_portable\", PRIMARY_MODEL, \"portable\"))\n            res = await run_batched([run_score(t) for t in ptasks], 500, \"score-head-pt\", client)\n            for r in res:\n                if r:\n                    zmap[(r[0], r[1])] = r[2]\n\n        # ---- 4. ABLATION (G!=S) on pilot slice, PORTABLE elicitation ----\n        ablation_raw = None\n        if do_ablation:\n            pilot = [d for d in docs if d.is_pilot] or docs  # fall back if none flagged\n            logger.info(f\"Ablation on {len(pilot)} pilot docs (portable elicitation)...\")\n            pilot_reals = [c for d in pilot for c in reals_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n            pilot_cf_nano = [c for d in pilot for c in cf_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n            # regenerate decoys with OTHER model (G=OTHER)\n            deco = await run_batched([gen_counterfactual_decoys(client, d,\n                                      reals_by_doc[d.doc_id], OTHER_MODEL,\n                                      random.Random(_doc_seed(d.doc_id, 31)))\n                                      for d in pilot], 64, \"decoy-other\", client)\n            cf_other_by_doc = {}\n            for d, dd in zip(pilot, deco):\n                decoys = (dd[0] if dd else [])\n                for x in decoys:\n                    x[\"cand_id\"] = f\"{d.doc_id}:cfo:{x['h']}>{x['t']}\"\n                cf_other_by_doc[d.doc_id] = decoys\n            pilot_cf_other = [c for d in pilot for c in cf_other_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n            pilot_swap = [c for d in pilot for c in swap_by_doc[d.doc_id]]\n\n            tasks = []\n            for cfg, model in [(\"nano_portable\", PRIMARY_MODEL),\n                               (\"ministral_portable\", OTHER_MODEL)]:\n                tasks += add_score_tasks(pilot_reals, cfg, model, \"portable\")\n                tasks += add_score_tasks(pilot_cf_nano, cfg, model, \"portable\")\n                tasks += add_score_tasks(pilot_cf_other, cfg, model, \"portable\")\n                tasks += add_score_tasks(pilot_swap, cfg, model, \"portable\")\n            res = await run_batched([run_score(t) for t in tasks], 400, \"score-abl\", client)\n            for r in res:\n                if r:\n                    zmap[(r[0], r[1])] = r[2]\n            ablation_raw = {\"pilot_docs\": [d.doc_id for d in pilot],\n                            \"cf_other_by_doc\": cf_other_by_doc}\n\n        elapsed = time.time() - t0\n        meta_runtime = {\"elapsed_s\": elapsed, \"cost_usd\": client.cost_usd,\n                        \"n_calls_live\": client.n_calls_live,\n                        \"n_calls_cached\": client.n_calls_cached,\n                        \"cached_tokens_observed\": client.cached_tokens_observed}\n        logger.info(f\"Pipeline done in {elapsed:.1f}s | cost=${client.cost_usd:.4f} | \"\n                    f\"live={client.n_calls_live} cached={client.n_calls_cached}\")\n\n    return {\n        \"docs\": docs, \"doc_by_id\": doc_by_id, \"reals_by_doc\": reals_by_doc,\n        \"all_reals\": all_reals, \"cf_by_doc\": cf_by_doc, \"swap_by_doc\": swap_by_doc,\n        \"zmap\": zmap, \"ext_meta\": ext_meta, \"ablation_raw\": ablation_raw,\n        \"contamination_rate\": contamination_rate, \"n_gen_decoys\": n_gen,\n        \"n_spont\": n_spont, \"n_true\": n_true, \"n_und\": n_und,\n        \"runtime\": meta_runtime,\n    }\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# ANALYSIS (offline, on collected Z)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ndef rank_normalize_config(pipe: dict, config: str, extra_cf: dict | None = None,\n                          docs: list | None = None) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"Per-doc rank-normalisation of all candidate Z for a scoring config.\n    Returns cand_id -> normalized Z. extra_cf: optional {doc_id: [cf_other cands]}.\n    docs: restrict to a document subset (default: all).\"\"\"\n    zmap = pipe[\"zmap\"]\n    norm = {}\n    for d in (docs if docs is not None else pipe[\"docs\"]):\n        pool = {}\n        cands = (pipe[\"reals_by_doc\"][d.doc_id] + pipe[\"cf_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]\n                 + pipe[\"swap_by_doc\"][d.doc_id])\n        if extra_cf:\n            cands = cands + extra_cf.get(d.doc_id, [])\n        for c in cands:\n            key = (config, c[\"cand_id\"])\n            if key in zmap:\n                pool[c[\"cand_id\"]] = zmap[key]\n        norm.update(st.rank_normalize(pool, SEED))\n    return norm\n\n\ndef certified_alphas(W: list[float]) -> list[float]:\n    out = []\n    for a in ALPHA_GRID:\n        T, n, _ = st.knockoff_plus_threshold(W, a)\n        out.append({\"alpha\": a, \"threshold\": (None if math.isinf(T) else T),\n                    \"n_admitted\": n, \"k_floor\": st.k_floor(a), \"certified\": n >= st.k_floor(a)})\n    return out\n\n\ndef analyze_s1(pipe: dict, norm_logprob: dict) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"S1 decoy signature: counterfactual (exchangeable) vs random-swap (anti-conservative).\"\"\"\n    docs = pipe[\"docs\"]\n    # build per-doc W lists for ALL reals (used for knockoff+ threshold) for each family\n    def family_pairs(family: str):\n        per_doc = {}\n        allpairs = []\n        for d in docs:\n            doc_pairs = []\n            cf = {c[\"real_id\"]: c[\"cand_id\"] for c in pipe[\"cf_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]}\n            sw = {c[\"real_id\"]: c[\"cand_id\"] for c in pipe[\"swap_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]}\n            for c in pipe[\"reals_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]:\n                zr = norm_logprob.get(c[\"cand_id\"])\n                if zr is None:\n                    continue\n                did = (cf if family == \"counterfactual\" else sw).get(c[\"cand_id\"])\n                if did is None:\n                    continue\n                zd = norm_logprob.get(did)\n                if zd is None:\n                    continue\n                rec = {\"zr\": zr, \"zd\": zd, \"label\": c[\"label\"], \"doc_id\": d.doc_id,\n                       \"w\": st.W_signed_max(zr, zd)}\n                doc_pairs.append(rec)\n                allpairs.append(rec)\n            per_doc[d.doc_id] = doc_pairs\n        return per_doc, allpairs\n\n    out = {}\n    for family in (\"counterfactual\", \"random_swap\"):\n        per_doc, allpairs = family_pairs(family)\n        W_all = [p[\"w\"] for p in allpairs]\n        false_pairs = [p for p in allpairs if p[\"label\"] == \"FALSE\"]\n        rows = []\n        for ainfo in certified_alphas(W_all):\n            a = ainfo[\"alpha\"]\n            T = ainfo[\"threshold\"]\n            if T is None:\n                rows.append({**ainfo, \"tail_win_rate\": None, \"n_tail\": 0})\n                continue\n            wr, n_tail = st.tail_win_rate([(p[\"zr\"], p[\"zd\"]) for p in false_pairs], T)\n            tail = [p for p in false_pairs if max(p[\"zr\"], p[\"zd\"]) >= T]\n            dz = [p[\"zd\"] for p in tail]\n            rz = [p[\"zr\"] for p in tail]\n            ks_s, ks_p = st.ks_two_sample(dz, rz, \"two-sided\")\n            mw_s, mw_p = st.mannwhitney(dz, rz, \"less\")  # decoy stochastically smaller?\n            # doc-block bootstrap of win-rate over FALSE pairs in tail\n            false_by_doc = {}\n            for p in tail:\n                false_by_doc.setdefault(p[\"doc_id\"], []).append(p)\n            units = list(false_by_doc.values())\n\n            def wr_fn(resample):\n                flat = [p for grp in resample for p in grp]\n                if not flat:\n                    return float(\"nan\")\n                return np.mean([1.0 if p[\"zd\"] > p[\"zr\"] else 0.0 for p in flat])\n            ci = st.doc_block_bootstrap(units, wr_fn, B=B_BOOT, seed=SEED)\n            rows.append({**ainfo, \"tail_win_rate\": (None if math.isnan(wr) else wr),\n                         \"win_rate_ci\": [ci[\"ci_low\"], ci[\"ci_high\"]],\n                         \"n_tail\": n_tail, \"ks_stat\": ks_s, \"ks_p\": ks_p,\n                         \"mw_stat\": mw_s, \"mw_p\": mw_p})\n        # robustness sweep at score quantiles over FALSE pairs\n        rob = []\n        if false_pairs:\n            maxz = np.array([max(p[\"zr\"], p[\"zd\"]) for p in false_pairs])\n            for q in (0.50, 0.75, 0.90):\n                thr = float(np.quantile(maxz, q))\n (None if math.isnan(wr) else wr), \"n_tail\": n_tail})\n        out[family] = {\"rows\": rows, \"robustness_sweep\": rob, \"n_false_pairs\": len(false_pairs)}\n    return out\n\n\ndef analyze_crux(pipe: dict, norm_logprob: dict) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"Spontaneous-error tail match: decoy ~ spont (want), decoy != truepos (want).\"\"\"\n    reals = pipe[\"all_reals\"]\n    cf_real = {c[\"real_id\"]: c[\"cand_id\"] for d in pipe[\"docs\"] for c in pipe[\"cf_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]}\n    F_truepos, F_spont, F_decoy = [], [], []\n    decoy_doc = {}   # doc_id -> list of decoy z (for bootstrap)\n    spont_doc = {}\n    for c in reals:\n        z = norm_logprob.get(c[\"cand_id\"])\n        if z is None:\n            continue\n        if c[\"label\"] == \"TRUE\":\n            F_truepos.append(z)\n        elif c[\"label\"] == \"FALSE\":\n            F_spont.append(z)\n            spont_doc.setdefault(c[\"doc_id\"], []).append(z)\n        did = cf_real.get(c[\"cand_id\"])\n        if did is not None:\n            zd = norm_logprob.get(did)\n            if zd is not None:\n                F_decoy.append(zd)\n                decoy_doc.setdefault(c[\"doc_id\"], []).append(zd)\n\n    pooled = np.array(F_truepos + F_spont + F_decoy)\n    regions = {}\n    region_defs = {\"full\": None, \"top50pct\": 0.50, \"top25pct\": 0.75}\n    for rname, q in region_defs.items():\n        if q is None:\n            dec, spo, tru = F_decoy, F_spont, F_truepos\n        else:\n            thr = float(np.quantile(pooled, q)) if pooled.size else 0.0\n            dec = [z for z in F_decoy if z >= thr]\n            spo = [z for z in F_spont if z >= thr]\n            tru = [z for z in F_truepos if z >= thr]\n        ks_ms, ks_mp = st.ks_two_sample(dec, spo, \"two-sided\")\n        mw_ms, mw_mp = st.mannwhitney(dec, spo, \"two-sided\")\n        ad_ms, ad_mp = st.anderson_darling_2samp(dec, spo)\n        perm_obs, perm_mp = st.permutation_two_sample(dec, spo, n_perm=4000, seed=SEED)\n        ks_ds, ks_dp = st.ks_two_sample(dec, tru, \"two-sided\")\n        mw_ds, mw_dp = st.mannwhitney(dec, tru, \"two-sided\")\n        gap = st.tail_gap(dec, spo)\n        # doc-block bootstrap of ks_sup(decoy, spont) using whole-doc resampling\n        units = [{\"d\": decoy_doc.get(did, []), \"s\": spont_doc.get(did, [])}\n                 for did in set(list(decoy_doc) + list(spont_doc))]\n\n        def kssup_fn(resample):\n            dd = [z for u in resample for z in u[\"d\"]]\n            ss = [z for u in resample for z in u[\"s\"]]\n            if not dd or not ss:\n                return float(\"nan\")\n            s, _ = st.ks_two_sample(dd, ss, \"two-sided\")\n            return s\n        gap_ci = st.doc_block_bootstrap(units, kssup_fn, B=B_BOOT, seed=SEED)\n        match_ok = (ks_mp > 0.05) and (mw_mp > 0.05)        # fail-to-reject decoy~spont\n        differ_ok = (ks_dp <= 0.05) or (mw_dp <= 0.05)      # reject decoy~truepos\n        # mean_diff = mean(decoy) - mean(spont). decoy HIGHER (>0) => decoys harder to\n        # reject than genuine errors => gate OVER-counts false discoveries => conservative.\n        # decoy LOWER (<0) => false reals beat their decoys => UNDER-count => anti-conservative.\n        verdict = (\"VALID\" if (match_ok and differ_ok)\n                   else (\"GAP:decoys_too_hard(conservative)\" if gap[\"mean_diff\"] > 0\n                         else \"GAP:decoys_too_easy(anti-conservative)\"))\n        regions[rname] = {\n            \"n_decoy\": len(dec), \"n_spont\": len(spo), \"n_truepos\": len(tru),\n            \"decoy_vs_spont\": {\"ks_p\": ks_mp, \"mw_p\": mw_mp, \"ad_p\": ad_mp,\n                               \"perm_meandiff\": perm_obs, \"perm_p\": perm_mp},\n            \"decoy_vs_truepos\": {\"ks_p\": ks_dp, \"mw_p\": mw_dp},\n            \"gap\": gap, \"gap_ks_sup_ci\": [gap_ci[\"ci_low\"], gap_ci[\"ci_high\"]],\n            \"verdict\": verdict,\n        }\n    grid = [round(x, 3) for x in np.linspace(0, 1, 101)]\n    figure_cdfs = {\"x\": grid,\n                   \"cdf_truepos\": st.empirical_cdf(F_truepos, grid),\n                   \"cdf_spont\": st.empirical_cdf(F_spont, grid),\n                   \"cdf_decoy\": st.empirical_cdf(F_decoy, grid)}\n    return {\"regions\": regions, \"figure_cdfs\": figure_cdfs,\n            \"n_truepos\": len(F_truepos), \"n_spont\": len(F_spont), \"n_decoy\": len(F_decoy),\n            \"populable\": len(F_spont) >= N_FALSE_MIN}\n\n\ndef analyze_ablation(pipe: dict) -> dict:\n    raw = pipe[\"ablation_raw\"]\n    if raw is None:\n        return {\"ran\": False}\n    pilot_ids = set(raw[\"pilot_docs\"])\n    extra_cf = raw[\"cf_other_by_doc\"]\n    configs = []\n    # (G, S): G in {nano(cf), other(cfo)}; S in {nano_portable, ministral_portable}\n    GS = [(\"nano\", \"nano\", \"nano_portable\"), (\"nano\", \"other\", \"ministral_portable\"),\n          (\"other\", \"nano\", \"nano_portable\"), (\"other\", \"other\", \"ministral_portable\")]\n    for (Gtag, Stag, scfg) in GS:\n        norm = rank_normalize_config(pipe, scfg, extra_cf=extra_cf)\n            else extra_cf.get(d.doc_id, []))\n            dec_by_real = {c[\"real_id\"]: c[\"cand_id\"] for c in decoys}\n            for c in pipe[\"reals_by_doc\"][d.doc_id]:\n                zr =          if zd is None:\n                    continue\n                pairs.append({\"zr\": zr, \"zd\": zd, \"label\": c[\"label\"], \"doc_id\": d.doc_id,\n                              \"w\":         (T if not math.isinf(T) else 0.0))\n        fb = {}\n        for p in false_pairs:\n            if max(p[\"zr\"], p[\"zd\"]) >= (T if not math.isinf(T) else 0.0):\n                fb.setdefault(p[\"doc_id\"], []).append(p)\n\n        def wr_fn(resample):\n            flat = [p for grp in resample for p in grp]\n            if not flat:\n                return float(\"nan\")\n            return np.mean([1.0 if p[\"zd\"] > p[\"zr\"] else 0.0 for p in flat])\n        ci = st.doc_block_bootstrap(list(fb.values()), wr_fn, B=B_BOOT, seed=SEED)\n        tail = [p for p in                   for p in pairs if p[\"label\"] in (\"TRUE\", \"FALSE\")]\n        diag = {str(a): st.decoy_gate_fdr(labelable, a) for a in ALPHA_GRID}\n        ci_cov = (ci[\"ci_low\"] <= 0.5 <=
